Capital city of Albania  
For the town in northern Italy, see [Tirano](/wiki/Tirano "Tirano").

<br />

| Coordinates: [41°19′38″N 19°49′07″E﻿ / ﻿41.32722°N 19.81861°E﻿ / 41.32722; 19.81861](https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Tirana&params=41_19_38_N_19_49_07_E_type:adm1st_region:AL_dim:100000) ||

**Tirana** ^[\[b\]](#cite_note-12)^ ([/tɪˈrɑːnə/](/wiki/Help:IPA/English "Help:IPA/English") [](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/0/07/En-us-Tirana.ogg/En-us-Tirana.ogg.mp3 "Play audio")^[ⓘ](/wiki/File:En-us-Tirana.ogg "File:En-us-Tirana.ogg")^ [*tih-RAH-nə*](/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key "Help:Pronunciation respelling key"),^[\[11\]](#cite_note-13)^^[\[12\]](#cite_note-14)^
Albanian pronunciation: [\[tiˈɾana\]](/wiki/Help:IPA/Albanian "Help:IPA/Albanian"); [Gheg Albanian](/wiki/Gheg_Albanian_language "Gheg Albanian language"): *Tirona* ) is the capital and [largest city](/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Albania "List of cities and towns in Albania") of [Albania](/wiki/Albania "Albania"). It is located in the centre of the country, enclosed by mountains and hills, with [Dajti](/wiki/Dajti "Dajti") rising to the east and a slight valley to the northwest overlooking the [Adriatic Sea](/wiki/Adriatic_Sea "Adriatic Sea") in the distance. It is among the wettest and sunniest cities in Europe, with 2,544 hours of sun per year.^[\[13\]](#cite_note-15)^^[\[14\]](#cite_note-currentresults.com-16)^{#cite_ref-currentresults.com_16-0}

Tirana was founded in 1614 by [Ottoman Albanian](/wiki/Ottoman_Albania "Ottoman Albania") general [Sylejman Pasha Bargjini](/wiki/Sulejman_Bargjini "Sulejman Bargjini"), centered on the [Old Mosque](/wiki/Sulejman_Pasha_Mosque "Sulejman Pasha Mosque") and *[türbe](/wiki/Sulejman_Pasha_Tomb "Sulejman Pasha Tomb")* . The site of present-day Tirana has been continuously inhabited since the [Iron Age](/wiki/Iron_Age "Iron Age") and was likely the core of the [Illyrian Kingdom](/wiki/Illyrian_kingdom "Illyrian kingdom") of the [Taulantii](/wiki/Taulantii "Taulantii"), which in [Classical Antiquity](/wiki/Classical_Antiquity "Classical Antiquity") was centred in the hinterland of [Epidamnus](/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs "Durrës"). Following the [Illyrian Wars](/wiki/Illyro-Roman_Wars "Illyro-Roman Wars"), it was annexed by [Rome](/wiki/Rome "Rome") and became an integral part of the [Roman Empire](/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire"); the heritage of that period is reflected by the [Mosaics of Tirana](/wiki/Tirana_Mosaic "Tirana Mosaic"). With the collapse of the [Western Roman Empire](/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire "Western Roman Empire") in the fourth century, most of Albania came under the control of the eastern [Byzantine Empire](/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"), as evident by the [Petrelë Castle](/wiki/Petrel%C3%AB_Castle "Petrelë Castle") built during the reign of [Justinian I](/wiki/Justinian_I "Justinian I"). The city was fairly unimportant until the 20th century, when the [Congress of Lushnjë](/wiki/Congress_of_Lushnj%C3%AB "Congress of Lushnjë") proclaimed it as Albania's capital after the [Albanian Declaration of Independence](/wiki/Albanian_Declaration_of_Independence "Albanian Declaration of Independence") in 1912.

Classified as a [gamma-world-city](/wiki/Global_city "Global city"),^[\[15\]](#cite_note-17)^ Tirana is the most important economic, financial, political, and trade centre in Albania due to its significant location in the centre of the country and its modern [air](/wiki/Air_transport "Air transport") and [road transportation](/wiki/Road_transport "Road transport").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ As the seat of power of the [Government of Albania](/wiki/Government_of_Albania "Government of Albania"), it hosts the official residences of the [President](/wiki/President_of_Albania "President of Albania") and [Prime Minister of Albania](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Albania "Prime Minister of Albania") and the [Parliament of Albania](/wiki/Parliament_of_Albania "Parliament of Albania"). The city was announced as the [European Youth Capital](/wiki/European_Youth_Capital "European Youth Capital") for 2022.{#cite_ref-17}  

History {#History}
------------------

See also: [Timeline of Tirana](/wiki/Timeline_of_Tirana "Timeline of Tirana")

|---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| ![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Americas.svg.png) | This section needs to be **updated** . Please help update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information. *(July 2020)* |

### Early development {#Early_development}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Tirana%2C_Albania_2017-04_Tirana_Mosaic_02.jpg/220px-Tirana%2C_Albania_2017-04_Tirana_Mosaic_02.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tirana,_Albania_2017-04_Tirana_Mosaic_02.jpg) The mosaics of an [Ancient Roman](/wiki/Tirana_Mosaic "Tirana Mosaic") house from the 3rd century AD

The area of Tirana has been inhabited by humans since prehistoric times with the earliest recognised reference found at the [Cave of Pëllumbas](/wiki/Cave_of_P%C3%ABllumbas "Cave of Pëllumbas") belonging to the Palaeolithic period. [Illyrians](/wiki/Illyrians "Illyrians") were the first population of the area and formed most likely the core of the [Illyrian kingdom](/wiki/Illyrian_kingdom "Illyrian kingdom") of the [Taulantii](/wiki/Taulantii "Taulantii"), which in classical antiquity was centered in the hinterland of [Epidamnus](/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs "Durrës").^[\[16\]](#cite_note-Hammond-18)^ When the Romans arrived in Illyria after their victory of the [Illyrian Wars](/wiki/Illyrian_Wars "Illyrian Wars"), they populated and integrated the area into their empire under the political control of the city of Rome. The oldest surviving discovery from this period is a [Roman house](/wiki/Tirana_Mosaic "Tirana Mosaic") dating to the 3rd century, which was transformed into an [aisleless church](/wiki/Aisleless_church "Aisleless church") with a mosaic floor. A [castle](/wiki/Fortress_of_Justinian "Fortress of Justinian"), possibly known as *Tirkan* , was built by the Byzantine Emperor [Justinian I](/wiki/Justinian_I "Justinian I") between the 4th and 6th century and later restored by Ahmed Pasha Toptani in the 18th century.^[\[17\]](#cite_note-Heppner1994-19)^{#cite_ref-Heppner1994_19-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Castillo_de_Petrela%2C_Petrela%2C_Albania%2C_2014-04-17%2C_DD_02.JPG/220px-Castillo_de_Petrela%2C_Petrela%2C_Albania%2C_2014-04-17%2C_DD_02.JPG)](/wiki/File:Castillo_de_Petrela,_Petrela,_Albania,_2014-04-17,_DD_02.JPG) [Castle of Petrelë](/wiki/Petrel%C3%AB_Castle "Petrelë Castle") was founded in the 6th century by [Justinian I](/wiki/Justinian_I "Justinian I").

Tirana is mentioned in [Venetian](/wiki/Republic_of_Venice "Republic of Venice") documents in the 1350s as well as in 1418: *"...the resident Pjeter, son of late Domenik from the village of Tirana..."* .^[\[18\]](#cite_note-Heppner2-20)^ Records of the first land registrations under the [Ottomans](/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") in 1431--32 show that Tirana consisted of 60 inhabited areas, with nearly 2,028 houses and 7,300 inhabitants.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ In 1510, [Marin Barleti](/wiki/Marin_Barleti "Marin Barleti"), an Albanian Catholic priest and scholar, in the biography of the Albanian national hero [Skanderbeg](/wiki/Skanderbeg "Skanderbeg"), *Historia de vita et gestis Scanderbegi Epirotarum principis* (*The story of life and deeds of Skanderbeg, the prince of Epirotes* ), referred to this area as a small village, distinguishing between "Little Tirana" and "Great Tirana".^[\[18\]](#cite_note-Heppner2-20)^ It is later mentioned in 1572 as *Borgo di Tirana* .^[\[19\]](#cite_note-21)^{#cite_ref-21}

According to [Hahn](/wiki/Johann_Georg_von_Hahn "Johann Georg von Hahn"), the settlement had already started to develop as a [bazaar](/wiki/Bazaar "Bazaar") and included several [watermills](/wiki/Watermill "Watermill"),^[\[20\]](#cite_note-Miho-22)^ even before 1614, when [Sulejman Bargjini](/wiki/Sulejman_Bargjini "Sulejman Bargjini"), a local ruler, built the [Old Mosque](/wiki/Sylejman_Pasha_Mosque "Sylejman Pasha Mosque"), a small commercial centre, and a [*hammam*](/wiki/Turkish_bath "Turkish bath") (Turkish bath). This is confirmed by oral sources, which state that there were two earlier mosques 300--400 m from the Old Mosque, towards today's [Ali Demi Street](/wiki/Ali_Demi_Street "Ali Demi Street"). The Mosque of Reç and the Mosque of Mujo were positioned on the left side of the [Lana River](/wiki/Lana_river "Lana river") and were older than the Old Mosque.^[\[20\]](#cite_note-Miho-22)^ Later, the [Et'hem Bey Mosque](/wiki/Et%27hem_Bey_Mosque "Et'hem Bey Mosque"), built by [Molla Bey of Petrela](/wiki/Molla_Bey_of_Petrela "Molla Bey of Petrela"), was constructed. It employed the best [artisans](/wiki/Artisans "Artisans") in the country and was completed in 1821 by Molla's son [Etëhem](/wiki/Et%C3%ABhem_Bey_Mollaj "Etëhem Bey Mollaj"), who was also Sulejman Bargjini's great-nephew.{#cite_ref-Miho_22-1}

In 1800, the first newcomers arrived in the [settlement](/wiki/Human_settlement "Human settlement")^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^, the so-called *ortodoksit* . They were [Aromanians](/wiki/Aromanians "Aromanians") from villages near [Korçë](/wiki/Kor%C3%A7%C3%AB "Korçë") and [Pogradec](/wiki/Pogradec "Pogradec"), who settled around modern day [Tirana Park on the Artificial Lake](/wiki/Tirana_Park_on_the_Artificial_Lake "Tirana Park on the Artificial Lake").^[\[21\]](#cite_note-23)^ They started to be known as the *llacifac* and were the first Christians to arrive after the creation of the town.^[\[22\]](#cite_note-24)^ In 1807, Tirana became the centre of the [Subprefecture](/wiki/Subprefecture "Subprefecture") of Krujë-Tirana.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ After 1816, Tirana languished under the control of the *Toptani* family of [Krujë](/wiki/Kruj%C3%AB "Krujë").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ Later, Tirana became a sub-prefecture of the newly created [Vilayet of Shkodër](/wiki/Vilayet_of_Shkod%C3%ABr "Vilayet of Shkodër") and the Sanjak of Durrës. In 1889, the [Albanian language](/wiki/Albanian_language "Albanian language") started to be taught in Tirana's schools,^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ and the patriotic club Bashkimi was founded in 1908.{#cite_ref-24}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Bazar_Tirana_%28ca._1900%292.jpg/220px-Bazar_Tirana_%28ca._1900%292.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bazar_Tirana_(ca._1900)2.jpg) The Old Bazaar at the turn of the 20th century. The [Sulejman Pasha Mosque](/wiki/Sulejman_Pasha_Mosque "Sulejman Pasha Mosque") is visible in the background. It was destroyed in [World War II](/wiki/World_War_II "World War II").  

### Modern development {#Modern_development}

On 28 November 1912, the national flag was raised in [Vlorë](/wiki/Vlor%C3%AB "Vlorë") by [President](/wiki/President_of_Albania "President of Albania") [Ismail Qemali](/wiki/Ismail_Qemali "Ismail Qemali"), marking the symbolic birth of Albania as a sovereign country. The next years, however, were marked by turmoil. During the [Balkan Wars](/wiki/Balkan_Wars "Balkan Wars"), Tirana was temporarily occupied by the Serbian army and it took part in uprising of the villages led by [Haxhi Qamili](/wiki/Haxhi_Qamili "Haxhi Qamili"). In August 1916, the first city map was compiled by the specialists of the Austro-Hungarian army.^[\[23\]](#cite_note-25)^ Following the capture of the town of [Debar](/wiki/Debar "Debar") by [Serbia](/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia "Kingdom of Serbia"), many of its Albanian inhabitants fled to [Turkey](/wiki/Turkey "Turkey"), the rest went to Tirana.^[\[24\]](#cite_note-Clayer306307-26)^ Of those that ended up in [Istanbul](/wiki/Istanbul "Istanbul"), some of their number migrated to Albania, mainly to Tirana where the Dibran community (people from [Dibër County](/wiki/Dib%C3%ABr_County "Dibër County")) formed an important segment of the city's population from 1920 onward and for some years thereafter.^[\[24\]](#cite_note-Clayer306307-26)^ On 8 February 1920, the [Congress of Lushnjë](/wiki/Congress_of_Lushnj%C3%AB "Congress of Lushnjë") proclaimed Tirana as the temporary capital of Albania, which had gained independence in 1912.^[\[25\]](#cite_note-Pearson-27)^ The city acquired that status permanently on 31 December 1925. In 1923, the first regulatory city plan was compiled by Austrian architects.^[\[26\]](#cite_note-28)^ The centre of Tirana was the project of [Florestano Di Fausto](/wiki/Florestano_Di_Fausto "Florestano Di Fausto") and [Armando Brasini](/wiki/Armando_Brasini "Armando Brasini"), well-known architects of the [Mussolini](/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini") period in Italy. Brasini laid the basis for the modern-day arrangement of the ministerial buildings in the city centre. The plan underwent revisions by Albanian architect Eshref Frashëri, Italian architect Castellani and Austrian architects Weiss and Kohler.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ The modern Albanian parliament building served as an officers' club. It was there that, in September 1928, [Zog of Albania](/wiki/Zog_of_Albania "Zog of Albania") was crowned King Zog I, King of the Albanians.{#cite_ref-28}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Old_villa_in_Tirana_city_center_01.jpg/220px-Old_villa_in_Tirana_city_center_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:Old_villa_in_Tirana_city_center_01.jpg) Old villa architecture in Tirana

Tirana was the venue for the signing of the Pact of Tirana between Fascist [Italy](/wiki/Italy "Italy") and Albania. During the rule of King Zog, many [Muhaxhirs](/wiki/Muhaxhir_(Albanians) "Muhaxhir (Albanians)") emigrated towards Tirana, which led to a growing population in the capital city in the early 20th century.^[\[27\]](#cite_note-29)^{#cite_ref-29}

In 1939, Tirana was captured by Fascist forces, who appointed a [puppet government](/wiki/Puppet_government "Puppet government"). In the meantime, Italian architect [Gherardo Bosio](/wiki/Gherardo_Bosio "Gherardo Bosio") was asked to elaborate on previous plans and introduce a new project in the area of present-day [Mother Teresa Square](/wiki/Mother_Teresa_Square_(Tirana) "Mother Teresa Square (Tirana)").^[\[28\]](#cite_note-30)^ A failed assassination attempt was made on [Victor Emmanuel III of Italy](/wiki/Victor_Emmanuel_III_of_Italy "Victor Emmanuel III of Italy") by a local resistance activist during a visit to Tirana. In November 1941, two emissaries of the [Communist Party of Yugoslavia](/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Yugoslavia "Communist Party of Yugoslavia") (KPJ), Miladin Popović and Dušan Mugoša, called a meeting of three Albanian communist groups ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ and founded the [Communist Party of Albania](/wiki/Party_of_Labour_of_Albania "Party of Labour of Albania"), and [Enver Hoxha](/wiki/Enver_Hoxha "Enver Hoxha") soon emerged as its leader.{#cite_ref-30}

The town soon became the centre of the Albanian communists, who mobilised locals against Italian fascists and later [Nazi](/wiki/Nazi "Nazi") Germans, while spreading ideological propaganda. On 4 February 1944, the [Gestapo](/wiki/Gestapo "Gestapo"), supported by the forces of [Xhafer Deva](/wiki/Xhafer_Deva "Xhafer Deva"), executed 86 anti-fascists in Tirana.^[\[29\]](#cite_note-31)^ On 17 November 1944, the [town was liberated](/wiki/Liberation_of_Tirana "Liberation of Tirana") after a [fierce battle between the Communists and German forces](/wiki/Albanian_Resistance_of_World_War_II "Albanian Resistance of World War II").^[\[30\]](#cite_note-32)^ The Nazis eventually withdrew and the communists seized power.{#cite_ref-32}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Tirana_Square_1988.jpg/220px-Tirana_Square_1988.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tirana_Square_1988.jpg) [Skanderbeg Square](/wiki/Skanderbeg_Square "Skanderbeg Square") in 1988, two years prior to the [Fall of communism in Albania](/wiki/Fall_of_communism_in_Albania "Fall of communism in Albania")

From 1944 to 1991, massive socialist-style apartment complexes and factories were built, while [Skanderbeg Square](/wiki/Skanderbeg_Square "Skanderbeg Square") was redesigned, with a number of buildings demolished. For instance, Tirana's former Old Bazaar and the [Orthodox](/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church "Eastern Orthodox Church") Cathedral were razed to the ground in order to build the Soviet-styled Palace of Culture. The northern portion of the main boulevard was renamed [Stalin](/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin") [Boulevard](/wiki/Zogu_I_Boulevard "Zogu I Boulevard") and his statue was erected in the city square. Because private car ownership was banned, mass transportation consisted mainly of bicycles, trucks and buses. After Hoxha's death, a [pyramidal museum](/wiki/Pyramid_of_Tirana "Pyramid of Tirana") was constructed in his memory by the government.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Before and after the proclamation of Albania's policy of self-imposed [isolationism](/wiki/Isolationism "Isolationism"), a number of high-profile figures paid visits to the city, such as Soviet leader [Nikita Khrushchev](/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev "Nikita Khrushchev"), [Chinese](/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China "People's Republic of China") Premier [Zhou Enlai](/wiki/Zhou_Enlai "Zhou Enlai") and [East German](/wiki/German_Democratic_Republic "German Democratic Republic") Foreign Minister [Oskar Fischer](/wiki/Oskar_Fischer_(politician) "Oskar Fischer (politician)"). In 1985, Enver Hoxha's funeral was held in Tirana.^[\[31\]](#cite_note-33)^ A few years later, [Mother Teresa](/wiki/Mother_Teresa "Mother Teresa") became the first religious figure^[\[32\]](#cite_note-34)^ to visit the country after the end of Albania's long [anti-religious](/wiki/Anti-religious "Anti-religious") [atheist](/wiki/State_atheism "State atheism") stance. She paid respects to her mother and sister resting at a local cemetery.{#cite_ref-34}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Albanien_%2805%29.jpg/220px-Albanien_%2805%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Albanien_(05).jpg) Tirana's main boulevard in 1991

Starting at the campus and ending at Skanderbeg Square with the toppling of Enver Hoxha's statue, the city saw [significant demonstrations](/wiki/Fall_of_communism_in_Albania "Fall of communism in Albania") by [University of Tirana](/wiki/University_of_Tirana "University of Tirana") students demanding political freedoms in the early 1990s. On the political aspect, the city witnessed a number of events. Personalities visited the capital, such as former U.S. Secretary of State [James Baker](/wiki/James_Baker "James Baker") and [Pope John Paul II](/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II "Pope John Paul II"). The former visit came amidst the historical setting after the fall of communism, as hundreds of thousands were chanting in Skanderbeg Square Baker's famous saying of "Freedom works!".^[\[33\]](#cite_note-35)^ Pope John Paul II became the first major religious leader to visit Tirana, though Mother Teresa had visited few years prior.{#cite_ref-35}

During the Balkans turmoil in the mid-1990s, the city experienced dramatic events such as the unfolding of the [1997 unrest in Albania](/wiki/1997_unrest_in_Albania "1997 unrest in Albania") and a [failed coup d'état](/wiki/Fatos_Nano#Second_and_third_premierships "Fatos Nano") on 14 September 1998.

In 1999, following the [Kosovo War](/wiki/Kosovo_War "Kosovo War"), Tirana Airport became a NATO airbase, serving its mission in the former Yugoslavia.  

### Contemporary {#Contemporary}

See also: [2018--2019 student protest in Albania](/wiki/2018%E2%80%932019_student_protest_in_Albania "2018–2019 student protest in Albania")  
Further information: [2019 Albania earthquake](/wiki/2019_Albania_earthquake "2019 Albania earthquake")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Streets_of_Tirana_2016.jpg/220px-Streets_of_Tirana_2016.jpg)](/wiki/File:Streets_of_Tirana_2016.jpg) Mustafa Matohiti Street near the [Pyramid of Tirana](/wiki/Pyramid_of_Tirana "Pyramid of Tirana"). After the [fall of communism in Albania](/wiki/Fall_of_communism_in_Albania "Fall of communism in Albania"), many areas saw new development.

During his term from 2000 to 2011, the former [mayor of Tirana](/wiki/Mayor_of_Tirana "Mayor of Tirana"), [Edi Rama](/wiki/Edi_Rama "Edi Rama"), undertook a campaign to demolish illegal constructed buildings across Tirana as well as along the river banks of [Lanë](/wiki/Lan%C3%AB "Lanë") to bring the area to its pre-1990 state. In an attempt to widen roads, Rama authorized the bulldozing of private properties so that they could be paved over, thus widening streets. Most main roads underwent reconstruction, including the Unaza, [Rruga e Kavajës](/wiki/Kavaja_Street "Kavaja Street") and the main boulevard. Rama also led the initiative to paint the façades of Tirana's buildings in bright colours, although much of their interiors continued to degrade. Rama's critics claimed that he focused too much attention on cosmetic changes without fixing any of the major problems such as shortages of drinking water and electricity.^[\[34\]](#cite_note-36)^^[\[35\]](#cite_note-37)^{#cite_ref-37}

In June 2007, [George W. Bush](/wiki/George_W._Bush "George W. Bush") traveled to Tirana on an official state visit, becoming the first [U.S. President](/wiki/U.S._President "U.S. President") to visit the former communist country.^[\[36\]](#cite_note-38)^^[\[37\]](#cite_note-39)^ In 2008, the [Gërdec explosions](/wiki/2008_G%C3%ABrdec_explosions "2008 Gërdec explosions") were felt in the capital as windows were shattered and citizens shaken. In January 2011, the [Albanian opposition demonstrations](/wiki/2011_Albanian_opposition_demonstrations "2011 Albanian opposition demonstrations") were triggered in front of the governmental buildings in Tirana protesting against political corruption and state capture, particularly associated with the former prime minister [Sali Berisha](/wiki/Sali_Berisha "Sali Berisha")'s government.^[\[38\]](#cite_note-40)^ In September 2014, [Pope Francis](/wiki/Pope_Francis "Pope Francis") made an official state visit to Tirana simultaneously becoming the second pontiff to visit Albania, after Pope John Paul II in 1992.^[\[39\]](#cite_note-Pope_Francis-41)^^[\[40\]](#cite_note-42)^{#cite_ref-42}

Following the municipal elections of 2015, power was transferred from the [Democratic Party](/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_Albania "Democratic Party of Albania") representative [Lulzim Basha](/wiki/Lulzim_Basha "Lulzim Basha") to the [Socialist Party](/wiki/Socialist_Party_of_Albania "Socialist Party of Albania") candidate [Erion Veliaj](/wiki/Erion_Veliaj "Erion Veliaj").^[\[41\]](#cite_note-43)^ Albania then underwent a territorial reform, in which defunct communes were merged with municipalities.^[\[42\]](#cite_note-44)^ Thirteen of Tirana's former communes were integrated as administrative units joining the existing eleven.^[\[43\]](#cite_note-:0-45)^ Since then, Tirana is undergoing significant changes in infrastructure, law enforcement and new projects, as well as continuing the ones started by Veliaj's predecessor. In their first few council meetings, 242 social houses got allocated to families in need.^[\[44\]](#cite_note-46)^ Construction permits were suspended until the capital's development plan is revised and synthesized.^[\[43\]](#cite_note-:0-45)^{#cite_ref-:0_45-1}

Between December 2018 and February 2019, a [series of demonstrations](/wiki/2018%E2%80%932019_student_protest_in_Albania "2018–2019 student protest in Albania") erupted in the central areas of Tirana and other cities of the country in response to a controversial law on higher education, poor quality of teaching, high tuition rates and corruption.^[\[45\]](#cite_note-47)^^[\[46\]](#cite_note-48)^^[\[47\]](#cite_note-49)^ In September 2019, Tirana was ravaged by a 5.6 [magnitude](/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale "Moment magnitude scale") [earthquake](/wiki/Earthquake "Earthquake") with an epicenter located near Durrës.^[\[48\]](#cite_note-50)^^[\[49\]](#cite_note-51)^^[\[50\]](#cite_note-52)^ Two months after, in November 2019, another strong [earthquake](/wiki/2019_Albania_earthquake "2019 Albania earthquake") with the magnitude of 6.4 hit the region again resulting in comparatively few damages in Tirana.^[\[51\]](#cite_note-53)^ The same month, Tirana was announced as the [European Youth Capital](/wiki/European_Youth_Capital "European Youth Capital") for 2022 with a planned program including events of cultural and social importance.^[\[52\]](#cite_note-54)^{#cite_ref-54}  

In December 2022, Tirana hosted the [EU-Western Balkans summit](/wiki/2022_EU-Western_Balkans_summit "2022 EU-Western Balkans summit"), marking the inaugural summit to be held outside the European Union's borders.^[\[53\]](#cite_note-55)^ On 21 September 2024, it was reported that [Prime Minister of Albania](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Albania "Prime Minister of Albania") [Edi Rama](/wiki/Edi_Rama "Edi Rama") was planning to create the [Sovereign State of the Bektashi Order](/wiki/Sovereign_State_of_the_Bektashi_Order "Sovereign State of the Bektashi Order"), a sovereign [microstate](/wiki/Microstate "Microstate") for the Order within Tirana.^[\[54\]](#cite_note-nyt_article-56)^{#cite_ref-nyt_article_56-0}  

Geography {#Geography}
----------------------

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/View_of_Tirana_from_the_Lapidar.jpg/220px-View_of_Tirana_from_the_Lapidar.jpg)](/wiki/File:View_of_Tirana_from_the_Lapidar.jpg) View of Tirana Metropolitan Area

Tirana extends at the [Plain of Tirana](/wiki/Tirana_plain "Tirana plain") in the centre of Albania between the mount of [Dajti](/wiki/Dajti "Dajti") in the east, the hills of Kërrabe, Sauk and Vaqarr in the south, and a valley to the north overlooking the [Adriatic Sea](/wiki/Adriatic_Sea "Adriatic Sea"). The average altitude is about 110 meters (360 ft) [above sea level](/wiki/Above_sea_level "Above sea level"), with a maximum of 1,828 metres (5,997 feet) at Maja Mincekut of Mali me Gropa in Shenmeri.^[\[55\]](#cite_note-57)^{#cite_ref-57}

The city is surrounded by two important [protected areas](/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Albania "Protected areas of Albania"): the [Dajti National Park](/wiki/Dajti_National_Park "Dajti National Park") and [Mali me Gropa-Bizë-Martanesh Protected Landscape](/wiki/Mali_me_Gropa-Biz%C3%AB-Martanesh_Protected_Landscape "Mali me Gropa-Bizë-Martanesh Protected Landscape"). In winter, the mountains are often covered with snow and are a popular retreat for the population of Tirana, which rarely receives snowfalls. In terms of [biodiversity](/wiki/Biodiversity "Biodiversity"), the forests are mainly composed of [pine](/wiki/Pine "Pine"), [oak](/wiki/Oak "Oak") and [beech](/wiki/Beech "Beech"), while its interior relief^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^ is dotted with [canyons](/wiki/Canyon "Canyon"), waterfalls, caves, lakes and other landforms.^[\[56\]](#cite_note-58)^ Thanks to its natural heritage, it is considered the "Natural Balcony of Tirana". The mountain can be reached by a narrow asphalt mountain road onto an area known as Fusha e Dajtit. From this small area there is a view of Tirana and its plain.{#cite_ref-58}

[Tiranë river](/wiki/Tiran%C3%AB_(river) "Tiranë (river)") flows through the city, as does the Lanë river. Tirana is home to several artificial lakes, including [Tirana](/wiki/Grand_Park_of_Tirana "Grand Park of Tirana"), Farka, Tufina, and Kashar. The present municipality was formed in the 2015 local government reform by the merger of the former municipalities of Baldushk, Bërzhitë, Dajt, Farkë, Kashar, Krrabë, Ndroq, Petrelë, Pezë, Shëngjergj, Tirana, Vaqarr, Zall-Bastar and Zall-Herr, which became municipal units. The seat of the municipality is the city of Tirana.^[\[6\]](#cite_note-Law_2014-6)^{#cite_ref-Law_2014_6-1}  

### Climate {#Climate}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Mali_Dajtit.jpg/220px-Mali_Dajtit.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mali_Dajtit.jpg) Snow at the [Dajti National Park](/wiki/Dajti_National_Park "Dajti National Park"). It generally melts quickly in the region.^[\[57\]](#cite_note-59)^

Tirana has a [humid subtropical climate](/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate "Humid subtropical climate") (*Cfa* ) according to the [Köppen climate classification](/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") and receives enough [precipitation](/wiki/Precipitation "Precipitation") during summer to avoid the [Mediterranean climate](/wiki/Mediterranean_climate "Mediterranean climate") (*Csa*) classification.

The average precipitation in Tirana is about 1,266 millimetres (49.8 inches) per year. The city receives the majority of precipitation in winter months, which occurs from November to March, and less in summer months, from June to September. In terms of precipitation, both rain and snow, the city is ranked among the wettest cities in [Europe](/wiki/Europe "Europe").^[\[14\]](#cite_note-currentresults.com-16)^{#cite_ref-currentresults.com_16-1}

Temperatures vary throughout the year from an average of 6.7 °C (44.1 °F) in January to 24 °C (75 °F) in July. [Springs](/wiki/Spring_(season) "Spring (season)") and [summers](/wiki/Summer_(season) "Summer (season)") are very warm to hot often reaching over 20 °C (68 °F) from May to September. During [autumn](/wiki/Autumn "Autumn") and [winter](/wiki/Winter_(season) "Winter (season)"), from November to March, the average temperature drops and is not lower than 6.7 °C (44.1 °F). The city receives approximately 2500 hours of sun.^[\[58\]](#cite_note-60)^{#cite_ref-60}  
{#cite_ref-62}{#cite_ref-68}

### Urbanism {#Urbanism}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Grand_Park_of_Tirana_%282020%29.jpg/220px-Grand_Park_of_Tirana_%282020%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Grand_Park_of_Tirana_(2020).jpg) The [artificial lake of Tirana](/wiki/Grand_Park_of_Tirana "Grand Park of Tirana") built from local waters in 1955

In September 2015, Tirana organized its first vehicle-free day, joining forces with numerous cities across the globe to fight against the existing problem of urban air pollution. This initiative resulted in a considerable drop in both air and noise pollution, encouraging the Municipality to organise a vehicle-free day every month.^[\[64\]](#cite_note-69)^^[\[65\]](#cite_note-70)^{#cite_ref-70}

The city suffers from problems related to [overpopulation](/wiki/Human_overpopulation "Human overpopulation"),^[\[66\]](#cite_note-71)^ such as [waste management](/wiki/Waste_management "Waste management"), high levels of [air pollution](/wiki/Air_pollution "Air pollution") and significant [noise pollution](/wiki/Noise_pollution "Noise pollution"). Over the last decades, air pollution has become a pressing concern as the number of cars has increased. These are mostly 1990s and early 2000s [diesel](/wiki/Diesel_engine "Diesel engine") cars,^[\[67\]](#cite_note-72)^ while it is widely believed that the [fuel](/wiki/Fuel "Fuel") used in Albania contains larger amounts of [sulfur](/wiki/Sulfur "Sulfur") and [lead](/wiki/Lead "Lead") than in the [European Union](/wiki/European_Union "European Union"). Effective 1 January 2019, the government has imposed an import ban of used vehicles made prior to 2005 in an effort to curb pollution, encourage the buying of new cars from certified domestic dealerships, and to improve overall road safety. Another source of pollution are PM10 and PM2.5 [inhaled particulate matter](/wiki/Atmospheric_particulate_matter "Atmospheric particulate matter") and [NO~2~](/wiki/Nitrogen_dioxide "Nitrogen dioxide") gases^[\[68\]](#cite_note-73)^^[\[69\]](#cite_note-74)^ resulting from rapid growth in the construction of new buildings and expanding road infrastructure.^[\[70\]](#cite_note-75)^{#cite_ref-75}

Untreated [solid waste](/wiki/Solid_waste "Solid waste") is present in the city and outskirts. Additionally, there have been complaints of excessive noise pollution. Despite the problems, the Grand Park at the Artificial Lake has some effect on absorbing CO~2~ emissions, while over 2.000 trees have been planted around sidewalks.

Works for four new large parks have started in the summer of 2015 located in Kashar, [Farkë](/wiki/Farka_Lake "Farka Lake"), Vaqarr, and [Dajt](/wiki/Dajti_Mountain "Dajti Mountain"). These parks are part of the new urban plan striving to increase the concentration of green spaces in the capital.^[\[71\]](#cite_note-76)^ The government has included designated green areas around Tirana as part of the Tirana Greenbelt where construction is not permitted or limited.^[\[72\]](#cite_note-77)^^[\[73\]](#cite_note-78)^{#cite_ref-78}  

Politics {#Politics}
--------------------

### Administration {#Administration}

Main article: [Units of Tirana](/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Tirana "Administrative divisions of Tirana")  
See also: [Neighborhoods of Tirana](/wiki/List_of_Tirana%27s_neighborhoods "List of Tirana's neighborhoods")  
Further information: [Mayor of Tirana](/wiki/Mayor_of_Tirana "Mayor of Tirana")  
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Minibashkit%C3%AB_in_Tirana_blank.svg/280px-Minibashkit%C3%AB_in_Tirana_blank.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Minibashkit%C3%AB_in_Tirana_blank.svg)  
[11](/wiki/Tirana_11 "Tirana 11")  
[10](/wiki/Tirana_10 "Tirana 10")  
[9](/wiki/Tirana_9 "Tirana 9")  
[8](/wiki/Tirana_8 "Tirana 8")  
[7](/wiki/Tirana_7 "Tirana 7")  
[6](/wiki/Tirana_6 "Tirana 6")  
[4](/wiki/Tirana_4 "Tirana 4")  
[3](/wiki/Tirana_3 "Tirana 3")  
[1](/wiki/Tirana_1 "Tirana 1")  
[2](/wiki/Tirana_2 "Tirana 2")  
[5](/wiki/Tirana_5 "Tirana 5")

The [municipality of Tirana](/wiki/Municipalities_of_Albania "Municipalities of Albania") is encompassed in the [County of Tirana](/wiki/County_of_Tirana "County of Tirana") within the [Central Region of Albania](/wiki/Central_Albania "Central Albania") and consists of the rural administrative units of [Baldushk](/wiki/Baldushk "Baldushk"), [Bërzhitë](/wiki/B%C3%ABrzhit%C3%AB "Bërzhitë"), [Dajt](/wiki/Dajt "Dajt"), [Farkë](/wiki/Fark%C3%AB "Farkë"), [Kashar](/wiki/Kashar "Kashar"), [Krrabë](/wiki/Krrab%C3%AB "Krrabë"), [Ndroq](/wiki/Ndroq "Ndroq"), [Petrelë](/wiki/Petrel%C3%AB "Petrelë"), [Pezë](/wiki/Pez%C3%AB "Pezë"), [Shëngjergj](/wiki/Sh%C3%ABngjergj "Shëngjergj"), [Vaqarr](/wiki/Vaqarr "Vaqarr"), [Zall-Bastar](/wiki/Zall-Bastar "Zall-Bastar"), [Zall-Herr](/wiki/Zall-Herr "Zall-Herr") and Tirana.^[\[74\]](#cite_note-Administration-79)^^[\[75\]](#cite_note-80)^ The [administrative unit of Tirana](/wiki/Administrative_units_of_Tirana "Administrative units of Tirana") is further partitioned into eleven urban administrative units, namely [Tirana 1](/wiki/Tirana_1 "Tirana 1"), [Tirana 2](/wiki/Tirana_2 "Tirana 2"), [Tirana 3](/wiki/Tirana_3 "Tirana 3"), [Tirana 4](/wiki/Tirana_4 "Tirana 4"), [Tirana 5](/wiki/Tirana_5 "Tirana 5"), [Tirana 6](/wiki/Tirana_6 "Tirana 6"), [Tirana 7](/wiki/Tirana_7 "Tirana 7"), [Tirana 8](/wiki/Tirana_8 "Tirana 8"), [Tirana 9](/wiki/Tirana_9 "Tirana 9"), [Tirana 10](/wiki/Tirana_10 "Tirana 10") and [Tirana 11](/wiki/Tirana_11 "Tirana 11").^[\[74\]](#cite_note-Administration-79)^{#cite_ref-Administration_79-1}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Bashkia_Tirane.jpg/220px-Bashkia_Tirane.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bashkia_Tirane.jpg) Tirana City Hall

The Mayor of Tirana along with the Cabinet of Tirana exercises executive power. The Assembly of Tirana functions as the city parliament and consists of 55 members, serving four-year terms. It primarily deals with budget, global orientations and relations between the city and the [Government of Albania](/wiki/Government_of_Albania "Government of Albania"). It has 14 committees and its chairman is Aldrin Dalipi from the Socialist Party. Each of the members have a specific portfolio such as economy, finance, juridical, education, health care, and several professional services, agencies and institutes.

In 2000, the centre of Tirana from the central campus of University of Tirana in the Mother Teresa Square up to the Skanderbeg Square, was declared the place of Cultural Assembly, and given state protection. The historical core of the capital lies around pedestrian only Murat Toptani Street, while the most prominent city district is [Blloku](/wiki/Blloku "Blloku"). In 2010, the municipality undertook the installing of street name signs and entrance numbers while every apartment entrance was physically stamped.^[\[76\]](#cite_note-81)^{#cite_ref-81}  

### National capital {#National_capital}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Tirana%2C_consiglio_dei_ministri%2C_01.JPG/220px-Tirana%2C_consiglio_dei_ministri%2C_01.JPG)](/wiki/File:Tirana,_consiglio_dei_ministri,_01.JPG) The [Kryeministria](/wiki/Prime_Minister%27s_Office_(Albania) "Prime Minister's Office (Albania)") at the [Dëshmorët e Kombit Boulevard](/wiki/D%C3%ABshmor%C3%ABt_e_Kombit_Boulevard "Dëshmorët e Kombit Boulevard") is the official office of the [Prime Minister of Albania](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Albania "Prime Minister of Albania").

Tirana is the [capital city](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") of the [Republic of Albania](/wiki/Republic_of_Albania "Republic of Albania") thus playing an essential role in shaping the political and economic life of the country.^[\[77\]](#cite_note-82)^ It is the home to government functions and institutions for which the government of Albania is responsible, as for instance the [executive](/wiki/Executive_(government) "Executive (government)"), [juridical](/wiki/Judiciary "Judiciary") and [legislative](/wiki/Legislative "Legislative") branches of Albania.{#cite_ref-82}

The President and [Prime Minister of Albania](/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Albania "Prime Minister of Albania") officially reside and work in Tirana specifically at the [Presidenca](/wiki/Presidential_Office_Building,_Tirana "Presidential Office Building, Tirana") and [Kryeministria](/wiki/Prime_Minister%27s_Office_(Albania) "Prime Minister's Office (Albania)"), respectively, nevertheless the [Parliament of Albania](/wiki/Parliament_of_Albania "Parliament of Albania") is headquartered at the [Dëshmorët e Kombit Boulevard](/wiki/D%C3%ABshmor%C3%ABt_e_Kombit_Boulevard "Dëshmorët e Kombit Boulevard").^[\[78\]](#cite_note-83)^^[\[79\]](#cite_note-84)^^[\[80\]](#cite_note-85)^ Tirana is also the home to the national [Constitutional Court](/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Albania "Constitutional Court of Albania") and [Supreme Court](/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Albania "Supreme Court of Albania"). Important national institutions housed in Tirana include the [Appeal Court](/wiki/Appeals_courts_of_Albania "Appeals courts of Albania") and [Administrative Court](/wiki/Administrative_Courts_in_Albania "Administrative Courts in Albania").{#cite_ref-85}

The [Bank of Albania](/wiki/Bank_of_Albania "Bank of Albania") is located at the Skanderbeg Square while other institutions such as the ministries of [Culture](/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_(Albania) "Ministry of Culture (Albania)"), [Defence](/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(Albania) "Ministry of Defence (Albania)"), [Education](/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Sports_and_Youth_(Albania) "Ministry of Education, Sports and Youth (Albania)"), [Finance](/wiki/Ministry_of_Finance_and_Economy_(Albania) "Ministry of Finance and Economy (Albania)"), [Foreign Affairs](/wiki/Ministry_for_Europe_and_Foreign_Affairs_(Albania) "Ministry for Europe and Foreign Affairs (Albania)"), [Health](/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_and_Social_Protection "Ministry of Health and Social Protection"), [Infrastructure](/wiki/Ministry_of_Infrastructure_and_Energy_(Albania) "Ministry of Infrastructure and Energy (Albania)"), [Internal Affairs](/wiki/Ministry_of_Internal_Affairs_(Albania) "Ministry of Internal Affairs (Albania)"), [Justice](/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice_(Albania) "Ministry of Justice (Albania)") and [Tourism](/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism_and_Environment_(Albania) "Ministry of Tourism and Environment (Albania)") are spread over Tirana. The city is also the home to all the consulates and embassies in Albania, thereby making it an important centre for international diplomacy in the country.  

### International relations {#International_relations}

See also: [List of twin towns and sister cities in Albania](/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Albania "List of twin towns and sister cities in Albania")

Tirana is a founding member of the Union of Albanian Municipalities in the Region.^[\[81\]](#cite_note-86)^^[\[82\]](#cite_note-87)^ Tirana is [twinned](/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities "Twin towns and sister cities") with [Ankara](/wiki/Ankara "Ankara"), [Beijing](/wiki/Beijing "Beijing"), [Bursa](/wiki/Bursa "Bursa"), [Doha](/wiki/Doha "Doha"), [Florence](/wiki/Florence "Florence"), [Kharkiv](/wiki/Kharkiv "Kharkiv"), [Sarajevo](/wiki/Sarajevo "Sarajevo") and has signed partnership agreements with [Verona](/wiki/Verona "Verona") and [Zagreb](/wiki/Zagreb "Zagreb").^[\[f\]](#cite_note-fn3-95)^^[\[90\]](#cite_note-96)^^[\[91\]](#cite_note-97)^ It has also signed special bilateral agreements with [Zaragoza](/wiki/Zaragoza "Zaragoza").^[\[92\]](#cite_note-98)^{#cite_ref-98}  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Banka_e_Shqip%C3%ABris%C3%AB_2017_03.jpg/220px-Banka_e_Shqip%C3%ABris%C3%AB_2017_03.jpg)](/wiki/File:Banka_e_Shqip%C3%ABris%C3%AB_2017_03.jpg) [Bank of Albania](/wiki/Bank_of_Albania "Bank of Albania")

Tirana is the heart of the [economy of Albania](/wiki/Economy_of_Albania "Economy of Albania") and the most [industrialised](/wiki/Industrialised "Industrialised") and economically fastest growing region in Albania. Of the main [sectors](/wiki/Sector_(economy) "Sector (economy)"), the [tertiary sector](/wiki/Tertiary_sector "Tertiary sector") is the most important for the economy of Tirana and employs more than 68% of work force of Tirana.^[\[93\]](#cite_note-sectors-99)^ 26% of the working population makes up the [secondary sector](/wiki/Secondary_sector "Secondary sector") followed by the [primary sector](/wiki/Primary_sector "Primary sector") with only 5%.^[\[93\]](#cite_note-sectors-99)^{#cite_ref-sectors_99-1}

The city began to develop at the beginning of the 16th century as it was part of the Ottoman Empire, when a bazaar was established, and its craftsmen manufactured silk and cotton fabrics, leather, ceramics and iron, silver and gold artefacts.^[\[94\]](#cite_note-100)^ In the 20th century, the city and its surrounding areas expanded rapidly and became the most heavily industrialised region of the country.{#cite_ref-100}

The most significant contribution is made by the tertiary sector which has developed considerably since the fall of communism in Albania. Forming the financial centre of the country, the [financial industry](/wiki/Financial_industry "Financial industry") is a major component of the city's tertiary sector and remains in good conditions overall due to [privatization](/wiki/Privatization "Privatization") and the commendable [monetary policy](/wiki/Monetary_policy "Monetary policy").^[\[95\]](#cite_note-101)^ All of the most important financial institutions, such as the Bank of Albania and the [Albanian Stock Exchange](/wiki/Albanian_Stock_Exchange "Albanian Stock Exchange") are centred in Tirana as well as most of the [banking companies](/wiki/List_of_banks_in_Albania "List of banks in Albania") such as the [Banka Kombëtare Tregtare](/wiki/Banka_Komb%C3%ABtare_Tregtare "Banka Kombëtare Tregtare"), [Raiffeisen Bank](/wiki/Raiffeisen_(Albania) "Raiffeisen (Albania)"), [Credins Bank](/wiki/Credins_Bank "Credins Bank"), [Intesa Sanpaolo Bank](/wiki/Intesa_Sanpaolo_Bank_(Albania) "Intesa Sanpaolo Bank (Albania)") and [Tirana Bank](/wiki/Tirana_Bank "Tirana Bank").{#cite_ref-101}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Plaza%2C_Tirane_Albania.jpg/220px-Plaza%2C_Tirane_Albania.jpg)](/wiki/File:Plaza,_Tirane_Albania.jpg) [Maritim Plaza Tirana](/wiki/Plaza_Hotel_Tirana "Plaza Hotel Tirana") is in the centre of Tirana.

The [telecommunication industry](/wiki/Telecommunication_industry "Telecommunication industry") represents another major and growing contributor to the sector.^[\[96\]](#cite_note-102)^ A rapid development occurred as well as after the end of communism and decades of isolationism mainly due to the new national policy of reform and opening up sped up the industry's development. [Vodafone](/wiki/Vodafone_Albania "Vodafone Albania"), [Telekom Albania](/wiki/Telekom_Albania "Telekom Albania") and [Eagle](/wiki/Eagle_Mobile "Eagle Mobile") are the leading telecommunication providers in Tirana, as in all the country.{#cite_ref-102}

The [tourism industry](/wiki/Tourism_industry "Tourism industry") of the city has expanded in recent years to become a vital component of the economy.^[\[97\]](#cite_note-103)^ Tirana has been officially dubbed as 'The Place Beyond Belief' by local authorities.^[\[98\]](#cite_note-104)^ The increasing number of international arrivals at the [Tirana International Airport](/wiki/Tirana_International_Airport "Tirana International Airport") and [Port of Durrës](/wiki/Port_of_Durr%C3%ABs "Port of Durrës") from across Europe, Australia and Asia has rapidly grown the number of foreign visitors in the city.^[\[99\]](#cite_note-105)^^[\[100\]](#cite_note-106)^{#cite_ref-106}

The largest hotels of the city are the [Tirana International Hotel](/wiki/Tirana_International_Hotel "Tirana International Hotel"), [Maritim Plaza Tirana](/wiki/TID_Tower "TID Tower") both situated in the heart of the city near Skanderbeg Square, and the Hyatt-owned luxury Mak Hotel Tirana^[\[101\]](#cite_note-107)^ located next to the [Air Albania Stadium](/wiki/Arena_Komb%C3%ABtare "Arena Kombëtare"), where Mariott Tirana Hotel is also planned to open.^[\[102\]](#cite_note-108)^ Other major hotels present in central Tirana include the Rogner Hotel, Hilton Garden Inn Tirana, Xheko Imperial Hotel, Best Western Premier Ark Hotel, and Mondial Hotel.{#cite_ref-108}  

Infrastructure {#Infrastructure}
--------------------------------

### Transport {#Transport}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Terminal_jashte.jpg/220px-Terminal_jashte.jpg)](/wiki/File:Terminal_jashte.jpg) The terminal of [Nënë Tereza International Airport](/wiki/Tirana_International_Airport_N%C3%ABn%C3%AB_Tereza "Tirana International Airport Nënë Tereza")  

#### Air {#Air}

Tirana is served by [Nënë Tereza International Airport](/wiki/Tirana_International_Airport_N%C3%ABn%C3%AB_Tereza "Tirana International Airport Nënë Tereza"), which is simultaneously the premier air gateway to the country. The airport was officially named in honour of the Albanian Roman Catholic nun and missionary, Mother Teresa. It connects Tirana with many destinations in different countries across Europe, Africa, and Asia. The airport carried more than 3.3 million passengers in 2019 and is also the principal [hub](/wiki/Airline_hub "Airline hub") for the country's [flag carrier](/wiki/Flag_carrier "Flag carrier"), [Air Albania](/wiki/Air_Albania "Air Albania").^[\[103\]](#cite_note-109)^{#cite_ref-109}  

#### Road {#Road}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Autobahn-Alb.jpg/220px-Autobahn-Alb.jpg)](/wiki/File:Autobahn-Alb.jpg) The [Rruga Shtetërore 2](/wiki/SH_2_(Albania) "SH 2 (Albania)") (SH2) connecting Tirana with [Durrës](/wiki/Durr%C3%ABs "Durrës")

The city's geographical location in the centre of Albania has long established the city as an integral terminus for the [national road transportation](/wiki/Roads_in_Albania "Roads in Albania"), thus connecting the city to all parts of Albania and the neighbouring countries.^[\[104\]](#cite_note-110)^ The [Rruga Shtetërore 1](/wiki/SH_1_(Albania) "SH 1 (Albania)") (SH1) connects Tirana with [Shkodër](/wiki/Shkod%C3%ABr "Shkodër") and [Montenegro](/wiki/Montenegro "Montenegro") in the north, and constitutes an essential section of the proposed [Adriatic--Ionian motorway](/wiki/Adriatic%E2%80%93Ionian_motorway "Adriatic–Ionian motorway"). The [Rruga Shtetërore 2](/wiki/SH_2_(Albania) "SH 2 (Albania)") (SH2) continues in the west and provides direct connection to Durrës on the Adriatic Sea. The Rruga Shtetërore 3 (SH3) is being transformed to the [Autostrada 3](/wiki/A3_(Albania) "A3 (Albania)") (A3) and follows the ancient [Via Egnatia](/wiki/Via_Egnatia "Via Egnatia"). It significantly constitutes a major section of the [Pan-European Corridor VIII](/wiki/Pan-European_Corridor_VIII "Pan-European Corridor VIII") and links the city with [Elbasan](/wiki/Elbasan "Elbasan"), Korçë and Greece in the south. Tirana is further connected, through the Milot interchange in the northwest, with [Kosovo](/wiki/Kosovo "Kosovo") following as part of the [Autostrada 1](/wiki/A1_motorway_(Albania) "A1 motorway (Albania)") (A1).{#cite_ref-110}

During the [communist regime in Albania](/wiki/Communism_in_Albania "Communism in Albania"), a plan for the construction of a [ring road](/wiki/Ring_road "Ring road") around Tirana arose in 1989s with no implementation until the 2010s.^[\[105\]](#cite_note-111)^ It is of major importance, especially concerning the demographic growth of the [metropolitan region](/wiki/Metropolitan_region "Metropolitan region") of Tirana as well as the importance of the economy. Although, constructions for the nowadays completed southern section of the ring road started in 2011, however, the northern and eastern sections are still in the planning process.^[\[106\]](#cite_note-112)^{#cite_ref-112}  

#### Rail {#Rail}

Rail lines of [Hekurudha Shqiptare](/wiki/Hekurudha_Shqiptare "Hekurudha Shqiptare") (HSH) connected Tirana with all of the major cities of Albania, including Durrës, Shkodër and Vlorë. In 2013, the [Tirana Railway Station](/wiki/Tirana_Railway_Station "Tirana Railway Station") was closed and moved to Kashar by the city government in order to create space for the New Boulevard ([Albanian](/wiki/Albanian_language "Albanian language"): *Bulevardi i Ri* ) project.^[\[107\]](#cite_note-113)^ The new Tirana Station will be constructed in [Laprakë](/wiki/Laprak%C3%AB "Laprakë"), which is projected to be a multifunctional terminal for rail, tram and bus transportation.^[\[108\]](#cite_note-114)^^[\[109\]](#cite_note-115)^ City officials have also talked about a light rail extension all the way to the location of the former rail station.^[\[110\]](#cite_note-Linja_e_re_hekurudhore-116)^ The new rail line from Tirana through Nënë Tereza International Airport to Durrës has started construction.^[\[110\]](#cite_note-Linja_e_re_hekurudhore-116)^{#cite_ref-Linja_e_re_hekurudhore_116-1}

In 2012, the Tirana municipality published a report according to which a project on the construction of two tram lines was under evaluation. The tram lines would have a total length of 16.7 kilometres (10.4 miles). The plan was never implemented. Under the plan, the two tram lines would have intersected in Skanderbeg Square. The public transport in Tirana is, for now, focused only in the city centre, so that the people living in the suburbs have fewer or no public transport connections.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^  

#### Bus {#Bus}

Tirana's bus network is its primary and only system of public transport. The system has 16 lines serving the urban core, with another 14 suburban lines serving its outer regions. The urban network is made up of 8 radial lines, 5 diagonal lines, and 3 circular or semi-circular lines.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan-117)^{#cite_ref-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan_117-0}

Busses often get stuck in traffic. There were only 7 kilometres (4.3 miles) of dedicated bus lines in 2020.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan-117)^{#cite_ref-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan_117-1}

There were 451 bus stops on the entire urban network in 2020, extending to over 170 kilometres (110 miles). Services operate every day, regardless of holidays and weekends, from 06:00 to 24:00. The entire network had an average [headway](/wiki/Headway "Headway") of 9 minutes on a daily basis in 2018 and in the first half of 2019.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan-117)^{#cite_ref-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan_117-2}

Nearly 257,000 residents lived within a 150 m (490 ft) walking area from a bus stop when surveyed in Tirana's strategic transport study in 2019. That was approximately 35% of the population living inside the Municipal unit of Tirana.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan-117)^{#cite_ref-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan_117-3}

A single-ride ticket costs 40 Lek, and no hourly or daily options are available. Disabled people and veterans may ride for free. An electronic ticketing system is under implementation.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan-117)^{#cite_ref-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan_117-4}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Tirana_Bikes.jpg/220px-Tirana_Bikes.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tirana_Bikes.jpg) An [Ecovolis](/wiki/Ecovolis "Ecovolis") station near [Mother Teresa Square](/wiki/Mother_Teresa_Square_(Tirana) "Mother Teresa Square (Tirana)")  

#### Cycling {#Cycling}

During the administration of mayor Erion Veliaj, the government of Tirana has significantly increased the creation and expansion of a [cycling infrastructure](/wiki/Cycling_infrastructure "Cycling infrastructure") in the city in order to reduce [traffic congestion](/wiki/Traffic_congestion "Traffic congestion") as well as to improve the [sustainable transportation](/wiki/Sustainable_transport "Sustainable transport").^[\[112\]](#cite_note-118)^^[\[113\]](#cite_note-119)^^[\[114\]](#cite_note-120)^ [Ecovolis](/wiki/Ecovolis "Ecovolis") was launched in 2011 offering rental services for [bicycles](/wiki/Bicycle "Bicycle") at different centrally located stations for a small fee.^[\[115\]](#cite_note-121)^^[\[116\]](#cite_note-122)^ The international [bicycle sharing system](/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system "Bicycle sharing system"), [Mobike](/wiki/Mobike "Mobike"), launched its operations on 8 June 2018 by deploying 4000 bicycles in the city.^[\[117\]](#cite_note-Mobike-123)^^[\[118\]](#cite_note-124)^ Both services are no longer available.{#cite_ref-124}

Safe cycling paths are still relatively rare, despite improvements in recent years. Paths are often blocked by parked cars or construction. Other obstructions which decrease ride quality, such as drain holes, are also prevalent. There were only around 30 kilometres (19 miles) of cycling routes in 2020.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan-117)^{#cite_ref-Sustainable_Urban_Mobility_Plan_117-5}  

### Education {#Education}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/AkademiaArteve.jpg/220px-AkademiaArteve.jpg)](/wiki/File:AkademiaArteve.jpg) The [University of Arts](/wiki/University_of_Arts_(Albania) "University of Arts (Albania)") at [Mother Teresa Square](/wiki/Mother_Teresa_Square_(Tirana) "Mother Teresa Square (Tirana)")

Tirana has the highest concentration of institutions of [tertiary education](/wiki/Tertiary_education "Tertiary education") in Albania, consisting of numerous [academies](/wiki/Academy "Academy"), [colleges](/wiki/College "College") and [universities](/wiki/Universities "Universities"). Most prominent among these is the University of Tirana with campuses around the city and more than 28,000 students from all backgrounds.^[\[119\]](#cite_note-Education-125)^ The [Polytechnic University of Tirana](/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_Tirana "Polytechnic University of Tirana") is another distinguished institution and also the most renowned engineering and technical university in the country. The four other public institutions in Tirana are the [University of Arts](/wiki/University_of_Arts_(Albania) "University of Arts (Albania)"), [University of Agriculture](/wiki/Agricultural_University_of_Tirana "Agricultural University of Tirana"), [University of Medicine](/wiki/University_of_Medicine,_Tirana "University of Medicine, Tirana") and [University of Sports](/wiki/Sports_University_of_Tirana "Sports University of Tirana").^[\[119\]](#cite_note-Education-125)^{#cite_ref-Education_125-1}

The educational system of Tirana has expanded substantially over the past years with the renovations of existing school facilities and the construction of new schools.^[\[120\]](#cite_note-126)^^[\[121\]](#cite_note-127)^ For [primary](/wiki/Primary_education "Primary education") and [secondary](/wiki/Secondary_education "Secondary education") education, a variety of schools are available, tagged with the public, private and international labels. Some of the international schools are the [Tirana International School](/wiki/Tirana_International_School "Tirana International School"), [Albanian International School](/wiki/Albanian_International_School "Albanian International School"), British School, Montessori School, Memorial School and World Academy. The public primary and secondary Servete Maçi School won an award at the 2020 [International Architecture Awards](/wiki/International_Architecture_Awards "International Architecture Awards").^[\[122\]](#cite_note-128)^{#cite_ref-128}  

### Health {#Health}

There are numerous public and private [hospitals](/wiki/Hospital "Hospital") as well as smaller public and private [health care facilities](/wiki/Health_care_facilities "Health care facilities") in the territory of Tirana. The [Mother Teresa University Hospital](/w/index.php?title=University_Medical_Centre_of_Tirana_%22Mother_Teresa%22&action=edit&redlink=1 "University Medical Centre of Tirana \"Mother Teresa\" (page does not exist)") is one of the largest medical tertiary institutions of the country. Other medical institutions include the [Shefqet Ndroqi University Hospital](/wiki/University_Hospital_%22Shefqet_Ndroqi%22 "University Hospital \"Shefqet Ndroqi\""), Koço Gliozheni Hospital, Mbretëresha Gjeraldinë Hospital and the [Military Hospital](/wiki/Tirana_Military_Hospital "Tirana Military Hospital").  

Demography {#Demography}
------------------------

|------|---------|---------|
| Source: ^[\[123\]](#cite_note-world-129)^^[\[124\]](#cite_note-130)^^[\[125\]](#cite_note-131)^^[\[126\]](#cite_note-132)^^[\[127\]](#cite_note-133)^^[\[128\]](#cite_note-134)^^[\[8\]](#cite_note-UnitPop-9)^ |||
[Historical population]

The [Institute of Statistics](/wiki/Institute_of_Statistics_(Albania) "Institute of Statistics (Albania)") (INSTAT) estimated the population of the municipality of Tirana at 598,176 in the 2023 census.^[\[7\]](#cite_note-FOOTNOTE2023_Albanian_census202467-7)^ With a population density of 502 people per square kilometre, Tirana is the most densely populated municipality in the country.^[\[3\]](#cite_note-PV-3)^ The encompassing [metropolitan area](/wiki/Metropolitan_area "Metropolitan area"), consisting of the regions of Durrës and Tirana, has a combined population of approximately 1 million amounting to nearly one third of the country's total population.^[\[129\]](#cite_note-census15-135)^{#cite_ref-census15_135-0}

Historically, Tirana has experienced a steady population increase in the past years, especially after the fall of communism in the late twentieth century as well as the beginning of the twenty-first century. The remarkable growth was, and still is, largely fueled by migrants from all over the country often in search of [employment](/wiki/Employment "Employment") and improved living conditions. Between 1820 and 1955, the population of Tirana tenfolded while during the period from 1989 to 2011, the city's population grew annually by approximately 2.7%. In the 19th and 20th centuries, the city had a rate of growth less than 1% annually until the 1970s, then down to less than 8% per year until the middle 20th century figures.^[\[130\]](#cite_note-136)^{#cite_ref-136}  
{#cite_ref-137}

| Religion in Tirana ^[\[131\]](#cite_note-137)^ |||||
|---|---|---|---|---|
|      ||   |      ||
| [Islam](/wiki/Islam "Islam") ||   | 55.7% ||
| [Orthodoxy](/wiki/Orthodoxy "Orthodoxy") ||   | 6.4% ||
| [Catholicism](/wiki/Catholicism "Catholicism") ||   | 5.4% ||
| [Bektashism](/wiki/Bektashism "Bektashism") ||   | 3.4% ||
| Other (mostly undeclared and [non-religious](/wiki/Non-religious "Non-religious")) ||   | 29.1% ||

Tirana's population is composed by a mixture of different cultural and ethnic groups from [Southern Europe](/wiki/Southern_Europe "Southern Europe"). The most represented ethnicities are Albanians (84.10%), Greeks (0.35%), Aromanians (0.11%), [Macedonians](/wiki/Macedonians_(ethnic_group) "Macedonians (ethnic group)") (0.07%) and [Italians](/wiki/Italians "Italians") (0.03%).^[\[132\]](#cite_note-138)^{#cite_ref-138}

In Albania, a [secular state](/wiki/Secular_state "Secular state") with no [state religion](/wiki/State_religion "State religion"), the freedom of [belief](/wiki/Freedom_of_belief "Freedom of belief"), [conscience](/wiki/Freedom_of_conscience "Freedom of conscience") and [religion](/wiki/Freedom_of_religion "Freedom of religion") is explicitly guaranteed in the [constitution of Albania](/wiki/Constitution_of_Albania "Constitution of Albania").^[\[133\]](#cite_note-139)^^[\[134\]](#cite_note-140)^ Tirana is religiously diverse and has many places of worship catering to its religious population whom are adherents of [Islam](/wiki/Islam "Islam"), [Christianity](/wiki/Christianity "Christianity") and [Judaism](/wiki/Judaism "Judaism") but also of [Atheism](/wiki/Atheism "Atheism") and [Agnosticism](/wiki/Agnosticism "Agnosticism"). They all maintain their Albanian headquarters spread across the territory of Tirana. Nevertheless, the [Bektashi Order](/wiki/Bektashi_Order "Bektashi Order") leadership established their world centre also in the city.{#cite_ref-140}

In the 2011 census, 55.7% of the population of the municipality of Tirana was counted as [Muslim](/wiki/Muslim "Muslim"), 3.4% as [Bektashis](/wiki/Bektashis "Bektashis") and 11.8% as Christian including 5.4% as Roman Catholic and 6.4% as [Eastern Orthodox](/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox "Eastern Orthodox").^[\[135\]](#cite_note-141)^ The remaining 29.1% of the population reported having no religion or did not provide an adequate answer. The census of 2011 did not included specific municipality level data for other religious groups. The [Roman Catholic Church](/wiki/Christianity_in_Albania "Christianity in Albania") is represented in Tirana by the [Archdiocese of Tiranë and Durrës](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Tiran%C3%AB-Durr%C3%ABs "Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Tiranë-Durrës"), with the [St Paul's Cathedral](/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Cathedral_(Tirana) "St Paul's Cathedral (Tirana)") as the seat of the prelacy. The [Albanian Orthodox](/wiki/Albanian_Orthodox_Church "Albanian Orthodox Church") community is served by the [Archbishop of Tirana](/wiki/Archbishop_of_Albania "Archbishop of Albania") in the [Resurrection Cathedral](/wiki/Resurrection_Cathedral,_Tirana "Resurrection Cathedral, Tirana").{#cite_ref-141}
