Culture {#Culture}
------------------

Main article: [Culture of Tirana](/wiki/Culture_of_Tirana "Culture of Tirana")  
[![The Albanians mosaic](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Mosaic_on_the_front_of_the_National_Historic_Museum_building_in_Tirana%2C_Albania%2C_20070720_img_1472.jpg/801px-Mosaic_on_the_front_of_the_National_Historic_Museum_building_in_Tirana%2C_Albania%2C_20070720_img_1472.jpg)](/wiki/File:Mosaic_on_the_front_of_the_National_Historic_Museum_building_in_Tirana,_Albania,_20070720_img_1472.jpg "Panorama of The Albanians History mosaic above the entrance of the National Museum of History")  
[](/wiki/File:Mosaic_on_the_front_of_the_National_Historic_Museum_building_in_Tirana,_Albania,_20070720_img_1472.jpg "File:Mosaic on the front of the National Historic Museum building in Tirana, Albania, 20070720 img 1472.jpg")  
Panorama of *The Albanians History* mosaic above the entrance of the [National Museum of History](/wiki/National_Museum_of_History_(Albania) "National Museum of History (Albania)")

Tirana offers a blend of traditional and modern lifestyle with a variety of arts, food, entertainment, music and night life. Its population celebrates a wide range of religious and other festivals including [Christmas](/wiki/Christmas "Christmas"), [Eid](/wiki/Islamic_holidays "Islamic holidays"), [Hanukkah](/wiki/Hanukkah "Hanukkah") and [Nowruz](/wiki/Nowruz "Nowruz"). Another festival is [Dita e Verës](/wiki/Summer_Festival,_Albania "Summer Festival, Albania") taking place every year on 14 March, during which the Albanians celebrate the end of winter and the arrival of spring.

Among the local institutions are the [National Library](/wiki/National_Library_of_Albania "National Library of Albania"), that keeps more than a million books, periodicals, maps, atlases, microfilms and other library materials. The city has five well-preserved traditional houses (museum-houses), 56 cultural [monuments](/wiki/Monuments "Monuments"), eight public [libraries](/wiki/Library "Library").^[\[136\]](#cite_note-142)^{#cite_ref-142}

There are many domestic and foreign cultural institutions in Tirana, amongst them the [British Council](/wiki/British_Council "British Council"), [Canadian Institute of Technology](/wiki/Canadian_Institute_of_Technology "Canadian Institute of Technology") as well as the German [Goethe-Institut](/wiki/Goethe-Institut "Goethe-Institut") and [Friedrich Ebert Foundation](/wiki/Friedrich_Ebert_Foundation "Friedrich Ebert Foundation").^[\[137\]](#cite_note-143)^^[\[138\]](#cite_note-144)^^[\[139\]](#cite_note-145)^^[\[140\]](#cite_note-146)^ Other cultural institutions include the Chinese [Confucius Institute](/wiki/Confucius_Institute "Confucius Institute"), Greek [Hellenic Foundation for Culture](/wiki/Hellenic_Foundation_for_Culture "Hellenic Foundation for Culture"), Italian [Istituto Italiano di Cultura](/wiki/Istituto_Italiano_di_Cultura "Istituto Italiano di Cultura") and the French [Alliance Française](/wiki/Alliance_Fran%C3%A7aise "Alliance Française").^[\[141\]](#cite_note-147)^^[\[142\]](#cite_note-148)^^[\[143\]](#cite_note-149)^^[\[144\]](#cite_note-150)^{#cite_ref-150}  

### Architecture {#Architecture}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Tirana%2C_Toptani_House_2015_01.jpg/220px-Tirana%2C_Toptani_House_2015_01.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tirana,_Toptani_House_2015_01.jpg) The Toptani house from the 18th century

Tirana is home to a mixture of architectural styles reflecting the influential periods in its history. Its current appearance was considerably shaped by two totalitarian regimes, once by the fascist regime of Benito Mussolini during the [Second World War](/wiki/Second_World_War "Second World War") and the regime of Enver Hoxha in the [aftermath](/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II "Aftermath of World War II"). The [Palace of Brigades](/wiki/Presidential_Palace,_Tirana "Presidential Palace, Tirana"), the ministries buildings, the government building and the municipality hall are designed by Florestano Di Fausto and Armando Brasini, both well-known architects of the Mussolini period in Italy. The Dëshmorët e Kombit Boulevard was built in 1930 and given the name [King Zog I](/wiki/Zog_I_of_Albania "Zog I of Albania") Boulevard.
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Tirana_panorama_2016.jpg/220px-Tirana_panorama_2016.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tirana_panorama_2016.jpg) [Florestano Di Fausto](/wiki/Florestano_Di_Fausto "Florestano Di Fausto") and [Armando Brasini](/wiki/Armando_Brasini "Armando Brasini") designed the city plan for Tirana in [Neo-Renaissance](/wiki/Neo-Renaissance_architecture "Neo-Renaissance architecture") style with articulate angular solutions and giant order fascias.

In the 20th century, the part from Skanderbeg Square up to the train station was named Stalin Boulevard. The Royal Palace or Palace of Brigades previously served as the official residence of King Zog I. It has been used by different Albanian governments for various purposes. Because of the outbreak of World War II, and the 1939 [Italian invasion of Albania](/wiki/Italian_invasion_of_Albania "Italian invasion of Albania"), Zog I fled Albania and never had a chance to see the Palace fully constructed. The Italians finished it and used it as the Army Headquarters. The Palace took its nickname Palace of Brigades because it was taken from the Italians by a people's army brigade.^[\[145\]](#cite_note-151)^{#cite_ref-151}

In the 21st century, Tirana turned into a proper modernist city, with large blocks of flats, modern new buildings, new shopping centres and many green spaces. In June 2016, the Mayor of Tirana Erion Veliaj and the Italian architect [Stefano Boeri](/wiki/Stefano_Boeri "Stefano Boeri") announced the start of the works for the redaction of the Master Plan *Tirana 2030* .^[\[146\]](#cite_note-152)^{#cite_ref-152}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/The_Grand_Park_of_Tirana_2016.jpg/220px-The_Grand_Park_of_Tirana_2016.jpg)](/wiki/File:The_Grand_Park_of_Tirana_2016.jpg) The entrance of the [Grand Park of Tirana](/wiki/Grand_Park_of_Tirana "Grand Park of Tirana")

Tirana is a densely-built area and still offers several public parks throughout its districts, graced with green gardens. The Grand Park is the most important green space in Tirana. It is one of the most visited areas by local citizens.^[\[147\]](#cite_note-153)^ The park includes many children's playgrounds, sport facilities and landmarks such as the [Saint Procopius Church](/wiki/Saint_Procopius_Church_of_Tirana "Saint Procopius Church of Tirana"), the [Presidential Palace](/wiki/Presidential_Palace_of_Tirana "Presidential Palace of Tirana"), the [Botanical Gardens](/wiki/Botanical_Gardens_of_Tirana "Botanical Gardens of Tirana"), the [Tirana Zoo](/wiki/Tirana_Zoo "Tirana Zoo"), the Amphitheatre, the Monument of the Frashëri Brothers and many others.{#cite_ref-153}

The [Rinia Park](/wiki/Rinia_Park "Rinia Park") was built during the Communist era. It bordered by Dëshmorët e Kombit Boulevard to the east, Gjergi Fishta Boulevard and [Bajram Curri Boulevard](/wiki/Bajram_Curri_Boulevard "Bajram Curri Boulevard") to the south, Rruga Ibrahim Rugova to the west and Rruga Myslym Shyri to the north. The [Taivani](/wiki/Taivani "Taivani") Centre is the main landmark in the park and houses cafés, restaurants, fountains, and a bowling lane in the basement. The Summer Festival takes place every year in the park, to celebrate the end of winter and the rebirth of nature and a rejuvenation of spirit amongst the Albanians.

As of 2020 it was announced that the Municipality of Tirana will build more green spaces and will plant more trees.^[\[148\]](#cite_note-154)^{#cite_ref-154}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Archaea_Tower%2C_Tirana%2C_Albania.jpg/220px-Archaea_Tower%2C_Tirana%2C_Albania.jpg)](/wiki/File:Archaea_Tower,_Tirana,_Albania.jpg) The Alban Tower, designed by Archea Associati (Italy), completed in 2021  

### Museums {#Museums}

Further information: [Museums in Tirana](/wiki/Category:Museums_in_Tirana "Category:Museums in Tirana")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Tirana%2C_Albania_%E2%80%93_National_Museum_of_History_2019_15.jpg/220px-Tirana%2C_Albania_%E2%80%93_National_Museum_of_History_2019_15.jpg)](/wiki/File:Tirana,_Albania_%E2%80%93_National_Museum_of_History_2019_15.jpg) The [National Museum of History](/wiki/National_Museum_of_History_(Albania) "National Museum of History (Albania)") at the [Skanderbeg Square](/wiki/Skanderbeg_Square "Skanderbeg Square")

Tirana is the home to a number of museums dedicated to a wide array of arts. The [National Museum of History](/wiki/National_Museum_of_History_(Albania) "National Museum of History (Albania)") is located at the Skanderbeg Square and the most representative museum of Tirana.^[\[149\]](#cite_note-155)^ The mosaic above the entrance is the most dominant feature of the museum displaying the story of how the [Albanian people](/wiki/Albanian_people "Albanian people") have fought against invasion and occupation throughout history.{#cite_ref-155}

Founded in 1948, the [National Museum of Archaeology](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Archaeology,_Albania "National Museum of Archaeology, Albania") at the Mother Teresa Square displays a wide collection of research and discoveries belonging to the archaeological locations around Albania.^[\[150\]](#cite_note-156)^ It exhibits span from prehistory through antiquity and the Middle Ages to the twentieth century, offering an overview of the country's historical diversity.{#cite_ref-156}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Reja%2C_Tirane_Albania.jpg/220px-Reja%2C_Tirane_Albania.jpg)](/wiki/File:Reja,_Tirane_Albania.jpg) The *Cloud Pavilion* outside the [National Art Gallery](/wiki/National_Art_Gallery_of_Albania "National Art Gallery of Albania") installed by Japanese artist [Sou Fujimoto](/wiki/Sou_Fujimoto "Sou Fujimoto")^[\[151\]](#cite_note-157)^

The [National Art Gallery](/wiki/National_Art_Gallery_of_Albania "National Art Gallery of Albania") is considered the most important gallery in Albania housing one of the greatest collections of paintings in the region.^[\[152\]](#cite_note-158)^ Located at the Dëshmorët e Kombit Boulevard, it holds approximately 4.500 works of art including the most important collection of [Albanian art](/wiki/Albanian_art "Albanian art") of the nineteenth and twentieth centuries.{#cite_ref-158}

The [Bunk'art Museum](/wiki/Bunkers_in_Albania "Bunkers in Albania") consists of two underground bunkers built under the orders and direction of Hoxha during the communist era. Located at the Fadil Deliu Street and Abdi Toptani Street respectively, the bunkers have been transformed into a history museum and contemporary art gallery with exhibits from the Second World War and [Cold War](/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War").^[\[153\]](#cite_note-159)^^[\[154\]](#cite_note-160)^{#cite_ref-160}

The [Museum of Secret Surveillance](/wiki/Museum_of_Secret_Surveillance "Museum of Secret Surveillance") was founded in 2017 and is housed within a twentieth century mansion, the building known as the *House of Leaves* , near the Dëshmorët e Kombit Boulevard.^[\[155\]](#cite_note-161)^ It commemorates and honours the victims who fell to the communist terrorism and violence during the communist period in Albania. Other museums include the [Natural Sciences Museum](/wiki/Natural_Sciences_Museum_of_Albania "Natural Sciences Museum of Albania"), which has branches in zoology, botany and geology, the former Enver Hoxha Museum and the Bunk'art Museum.{#cite_ref-161}

The [Bektashi Museum](/wiki/Bektashi_Museum "Bektashi Museum") was opened at the [World Headquarters of the Bektashi](/wiki/World_Headquarters_of_the_Bektashi "World Headquarters of the Bektashi") on 7 September 2015. The museum contains exhibits relating to Bektashi history and leadership.^[\[156\]](#cite_note-162)^{#cite_ref-162}  

### Cuisine {#Cuisine}

As in other parts of Albania, agricultural traditions are of great significance to the Albanians in Tirana, substantially appreciated for the production of food such as cheese, olives and wine. In 2016, Albania surpassed Spain by becoming the country with the most coffee houses per capita in the world with 654 coffee houses per 100,000 inhabitants.^[\[157\]](#cite_note-163)^ This is due to coffee houses closing down in Spain due to the economic crisis, and the fact that as many cafes open as they close in Albania. In addition, the fact that it was one of the easiest ways to make a living after the fall of communism in Albania, together with the country's Ottoman legacy further reinforce its strong dominance in Albania.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-163}

The Tirana region is known for the Fergesa traditional dish made with either peppers or liver,^[\[158\]](#cite_note-164)^ and is found at a number of traditional restaurants in the city and agri-tourism sites on the outskirts of Tirana.{#cite_ref-164}  

### Sports {#Sports}

Being the capital, Tirana is the centre of sport in Albania, where activity is organised across amateur and professional levels. It is home to many major sporting facilities. Starting from 2007, the Tirana Municipality has built up to 80 sport gardens in most of Tirana's neighborhoods. One of the latest projects is the reconstruction of the existing [Olympic Park](/wiki/Tirana_Olympic_Park "Tirana Olympic Park"), that will provide infrastructure for most intramural sports.^[\[159\]](#cite_note-165)^{#cite_ref-165}

Tirana hosted in the past three major events, the [2006 European Promotion Cup for Men](/wiki/2006_European_Promotion_Cup_for_Men "2006 European Promotion Cup for Men"), [2011 World Mountain Running Championships](/wiki/2011_World_Mountain_Running_Championships "2011 World Mountain Running Championships") and the [2013 European Weightlifting Championships](/wiki/2013_European_Weightlifting_Championships "2013 European Weightlifting Championships").
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Muzeu_Arkeologjike_Tirane.jpg/220px-Muzeu_Arkeologjike_Tirane.jpg)](/wiki/File:Muzeu_Arkeologjike_Tirane.jpg) [Air Albania Stadium](/wiki/National_Arena_Stadium "National Arena Stadium") in the city centre under construction

There are two major stadiums, the former [Qemal Stafa Stadium](/wiki/Qemal_Stafa_Stadium "Qemal Stafa Stadium") and the [Selman Stërmasi stadium](/wiki/Selman_St%C3%ABrmasi_stadium "Selman Stërmasi stadium"). The former was demolished in 2016 to make way for the new national stadium.^[\[160\]](#cite_note-166)^ The new stadium called the *[Air Albania Stadium](/wiki/National_Arena_Stadium "National Arena Stadium")* was constructed on the same site of the former Qemal Stafa Stadium and it is planned to open in late 2019. It will have an underground parking, Marriott Tirana Hotel, shops and bars and will be used for entertainment events. Tirana's sports infrastructure is developing fast because of the investments from the municipality and the [government](/wiki/Ministry_of_Tourism,_Cultural_Affairs,_Youth_and_Sports_(Albania) "Ministry of Tourism, Cultural Affairs, Youth and Sports (Albania)").{#cite_ref-166}

[Football](/wiki/Football_in_Albania "Football in Albania") is the most widely followed sport in Tirana as well as in the country, having numerous club teams including the [KF Tirana](/wiki/KF_Tirana "KF Tirana"), [Partizani Tirana](/wiki/Partizani_Tirana "Partizani Tirana"), and [Dinamo Tirana](/wiki/Dinamo_Tirana "Dinamo Tirana"). It is popular at every level of society, from children to wealthy professionals. In football, as of April 2012, the Tirana-based teams have won a combined [57 championships](/wiki/List_of_Albanian_football_champions "List of Albanian football champions") out of 72 championships organised by the [FSHF](/wiki/FSHF "FSHF"), i.e. 79% of them. Another popular sport in Albania is basketball, represented in particular by the teams [KB Tirana](/wiki/KB_Tirana "KB Tirana"), [BC Partizani](/wiki/BC_Partizani_Tirana "BC Partizani Tirana"), [BC Dinamo](/wiki/BC_Dinamo_Tirana "BC Dinamo Tirana"), [Ardhmëria](/wiki/Ardhm%C3%ABria_Basket "Ardhmëria Basket") and also the women's [PBC Tirana](/wiki/PBC_Tirana_(women) "PBC Tirana (women)").

Recently two [rugby teams](/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Albania "Rugby union in Albania") were created: [Tirana Rugby Club](/wiki/Tirana_Rugby_Club "Tirana Rugby Club"),^[\[161\]](#cite_note-167)^ founded in 2013 and Ilirët Rugby Club^[\[162\]](#cite_note-168)^ founded in 2016.{#cite_ref-168}  

### Media {#Media}

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Villa_of_the_former_Radio_Tirana_%2803%29.jpg/220px-Villa_of_the_former_Radio_Tirana_%2803%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Villa_of_the_former_Radio_Tirana_(03).jpg) The former grounds of the headquarters of [Radio Tirana](/wiki/Radio_Tirana "Radio Tirana"). Radio Televizioni Shqiptar (RTSH) was initially founded as Radio Tirana in 1938.

As the capital, Tirana is the most significant location for the Albanian media industry whose content is distributed throughout Albania, Kosovo and other Albanian-speaking territories. Tirana is the home to most of the national and international [television stations](/wiki/Television_station "Television station"), including the national broadcaster, [Radio Televizioni Shqiptar](/wiki/Radio_Televizioni_Shqiptar "Radio Televizioni Shqiptar") (RTSH), along with all its television and radio networks. The three largest Albanian commercial broadcasters, such as [Televizioni Klan](/wiki/TV_Klan "TV Klan"), [Top Channel](/wiki/Top_Channel "Top Channel") and [Vizion Plus](/wiki/Vizion_Plus "Vizion Plus"), also maintains their headquarters in the city. The European broadcaster, [Euronews](/wiki/Euronews "Euronews"), operates a franchise in the city as well as the American broadcaster [CNN](/wiki/CNN_International "CNN International").^[\[163\]](#cite_note-169)^^[\[164\]](#cite_note-170)^{#cite_ref-170}

Tirana is also a principal location for the largest Albanian newspapers, magazines and publications. The newspapers with the largest circulations in Albania are published in Tirana, including [Gazeta Shqip](/wiki/Gazeta_Shqip "Gazeta Shqip"), [Gazeta Tema](/wiki/Gazeta_Tema "Gazeta Tema"), [Koha Jonë](/wiki/Koha_Jon%C3%AB "Koha Jonë") and Panorama. [Gazeta Shqiptare](/wiki/Gazeta_Shqiptare "Gazeta Shqiptare"), one of the oldest Albanian-language newspapers in Albania, operates and has its headquarters in the city.^[\[165\]](#cite_note-171)^ Tirana also has a well-established [English-language](/wiki/English_language "English language") newspaper, notably the daily of [Tirana Times](/wiki/Tirana_Times "Tirana Times").{#cite_ref-171}  

Notable people {#Notable_people}
--------------------------------

Main article: [List of people from Tirana](/wiki/List_of_people_from_Tirana "List of people from Tirana")  

### Key of Tirana {#Key_of_Tirana}

The *Key of Tirana* ([Albanian](/wiki/Albanian_language "Albanian language"): *Çelësi i Qytetit*) is a symbolic recognition given by the Mayor of Tirana to an esteemed personality. It was given to:  
* [Atifete Jahjaga](/wiki/Atifete_Jahjaga "Atifete Jahjaga"), Kosovo-Albanian politician and activist^[\[166\]](#cite_note-172)^{#cite_ref-172}
* [Bebe Rexha](/wiki/Bebe_Rexha "Bebe Rexha"), Albanian-American singer and songwriter^[\[167\]](#cite_note-Bebe_Rexha_and_Fatboy_Slim-173)^{#cite_ref-Bebe_Rexha_and_Fatboy_Slim_173-0}
* [Dritan Abazović](/wiki/Dritan_Abazovi%C4%87 "Dritan Abazović"), Montenegrin-Albanian politician^[\[168\]](#cite_note-174)^{#cite_ref-174}
* [Dua Lipa](/wiki/Dua_Lipa "Dua Lipa"), English-Albanian singer and songwriter^[\[169\]](#cite_note-175)^{#cite_ref-175}
* [Eleni Foureira](/wiki/Eleni_Foureira "Eleni Foureira"), Greek-Albanian singer^[\[170\]](#cite_note-176)^{#cite_ref-176}
* [Emeli Sandé](/wiki/Emeli_Sand%C3%A9 "Emeli Sandé"), Scottish singer and songwriter^[\[171\]](#cite_note-177)^{#cite_ref-177}
* [Ermal Meta](/wiki/Ermal_Meta "Ermal Meta"), Italian-Albanian singer and songwriter^[\[172\]](#cite_note-178)^{#cite_ref-178}
* Giorgio Toschi, Italian commander^[\[173\]](#cite_note-179)^{#cite_ref-179}
* [Giusy Ferreri](/wiki/Giusy_Ferreri "Giusy Ferreri"), Italian singer and songwriter^[\[174\]](#cite_note-180)^{#cite_ref-180}
* [Fatboy Slim](/wiki/Fatboy_Slim "Fatboy Slim"), English musician^[\[167\]](#cite_note-Bebe_Rexha_and_Fatboy_Slim-173)^{#cite_ref-Bebe_Rexha_and_Fatboy_Slim_173-1}
* [István Tarlós](/wiki/Istv%C3%A1n_Tarl%C3%B3s "István Tarlós"), Hungarian politician^[\[175\]](#cite_note-181)^{#cite_ref-181}
* [Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović](/wiki/Kolinda_Grabar-Kitarovi%C4%87 "Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović"), Former Croatian president^[\[176\]](#cite_note-182)^{#cite_ref-182}
* [Nexhmije Pagarusha](/wiki/Nexhmije_Pagarusha "Nexhmije Pagarusha"), Kosovo-Albanian icon and singer^[\[177\]](#cite_note-183)^{#cite_ref-183}
* [Noel Malcolm](/wiki/Noel_Malcolm "Noel Malcolm"), English journalist and historian^[\[178\]](#cite_note-184)^{#cite_ref-184}
* [Riccardo Cocciante](/wiki/Riccardo_Cocciante "Riccardo Cocciante"), Italian singer and songwriter^[\[179\]](#cite_note-185)^{#cite_ref-185}
* [Rita Ora](/wiki/Rita_Ora "Rita Ora"), British-Albanian singer and songwriter^[\[180\]](#cite_note-186)^{#cite_ref-186}
* [Robin Krasniqi](/wiki/Robin_Krasniqi "Robin Krasniqi"), German-Albanian boxer^[\[181\]](#cite_note-187)^{#cite_ref-187}
* [Stevo Pendarovski](/wiki/Stevo_Pendarovski "Stevo Pendarovski"), Macedonian politician^[\[182\]](#cite_note-188)^{#cite_ref-188}
